data-icon-position="" data-hide-link-title="0">View inline</a></li><li class="view-popup"><a href="/highwire/markup/1030681/expansion?width=1000&amp;height=500&amp;iframe=true&amp;postprocessors=highwire_tables%2Chighwire_reclass%2Chighwire_figures%2Chighwire_math%2Chighwire_inline_linked_media%2Chighwire_embed" class="colorbox colorbox-load table-expand-popup" rel="gallery-fragment-tables" data-icon-position="" data-hide-link-title="0">View popup</a></li><li class="download-ppt last"><a href="/highwire/powerpoint/1030681" class="highwire-figure-link highwire-figure-link-ppt" data-icon-position="" data-hide-link-title="0">Download powerpoint</a></li></ul></div></div><div class="table-caption"><span class="table-label">Table 2.</span> <span class="caption-title">Summary of <em>BLOC1S1</em> variant cellular phenotypes.</span><div class="sb-div caption-clear"></div></div></div><div id="T3" class="table pos-float"><div class="table-inline table-callout-links"><div class="callout"><span>View this table:</span><ul class="callout-links"><li class="view-inline first"><a href="" class="table-expand-inline" data-table-url="/highwire/markup/1030686/expansion?postprocessors=highwire_tables%2Chighwire_reclass%2Chighwire_figures%2Chighwire_math%2Chighwire_inline_linked_media%2Chighwire_embed&amp;table-expand-inline=1" data-icon-position="" data-hide-link-title="0">View inline</a></li><li class="view-popup"><a href="/highwire/markup/1030686/expansion?width=1000&amp;height=500&amp;iframe=true&amp;postprocessors=highwire_tables%2Chighwire_reclass%2Chighwire_figures%2Chighwire_math%2Chighwire_inline_linked_media%2Chighwire_embed" class="colorbox colorbox-load table-expand-popup" rel="gallery-fragment-tables" data-icon-position="" data-hide-link-title="0">View popup</a></li><li class="download-ppt last"><a href="/highwire/powerpoint/1030686" class="highwire-figure-link highwire-figure-link-ppt" data-icon-position="" data-hide-link-title="0">Download powerpoint</a></li></ul></div></div><div class="table-caption"><span class="table-label">Table 3.</span> <span class="caption-title">Summary of <em>BLOC1S1</em> variant classification.</span><div class="sb-div caption-clear"></div></div></div></div><div id="sec-21" class="subsection"><h3>Effects of <em>BLOC1S1</em> KO or variants in a melanocytic cell line</h3><p id="p-60">Whereas KO or LoF variants in <em>BLOC1S1</em> orthologs in mouse,<sup><a id="xref-ref-56-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-56">56</a></sup> Drosophila,<sup><a id="xref-ref-57-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-57">57</a></sup> and zebrafish<sup><a id="xref-ref-58-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-58">58</a></sup> cause defective pigmentation, this has not been demonstrated in humans. A pale skin relative to family members (FI:1), hypopigmentation (FVII:1), and ocular findings consistent with ocular albinism (FIII:1 and FV:2) were observed in some of the individuals harboring <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants reported here, but these pigmentation defects are milder than those in HPS. To analyze the role of BLOC1S1 in human pigmentation, we used CRISPR-Cas9 to KO <em>BLOC1S1</em> in MNT-1 cells (<a id="xref-fig-7-1" class="xref-fig" href="#F7">Figure 7A</a>), a human melanocytic cell line commonly used in studies of pigmentation.<sup><a id="xref-ref-59-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-59">59</a></sup> We observed that <em>BLOC1S1</em>-KO MNT-1 cells had no detectable BLOC1S1 protein (<a id="xref-fig-7-2" class="xref-fig" href="#F7">Figure 7A</a>). These cells exhibited reduced melanin content relative to WT MNT-1 cells, as assessed by the lighter color of cell pellets (<a id="xref-fig-7-3" class="xref-fig" href="#F7">Figure 7B</a>), decreased side-scatter (SSC) by flow cytometry (<a id="xref-fig-7-4" class="xref-fig" href="#F7">Figure 7C and D</a>),<sup><a id="xref-ref-29-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-29">29</a></sup> and decreased absorbance of cell extracts at 405 nm detected by spectrophotometry (<a id="xref-fig-7-5" class="xref-fig" href="#F7">Figure 7E</a>, two leftmost columns). Since the spectrophotometry assay was more sensitive to detect differences between <em>BLOC1S1</em>-KO and WT cells, we used it to assess the activity of the E49*, L62P, H69P, A95D, and G120E variants. This was done by infecting <em>BLOC1S1</em>-KO MNT-1 cells with viruses encoding the different variants, and measuring melanin content. The results showed that expression of all <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants rescued melanin content in <em>BLOC1S1</em>-KO cells, completely in the case of L62P, H69P, A95D or A115S <em>BLOC1S1</em> and partially in the case of G120D and E49* <em>BLOC1S1</em> (<a id="xref-fig-7-6" class="xref-fig" href="#F7">Figure 7E</a>). Therefore, most of the variants are more defective in BORC-related functions (<a id="xref-fig-5-4" class="xref-fig" href="#F5">Figures 5</a> and <a id="xref-fig-6-2" class="xref-fig" href="#F6">6</a>) than BLOC-1-related functions (<a id="xref-fig-7-7" class="xref-fig" href="#F7">Figure 7</a>), consistent with the clinical presentation of the <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants as a neurological disorder with little or no evidence of reduced pigmentation.</p><div id="F7" class="fig pos-float type-figure  odd"><div class="highwire-figure"><div class="fig-inline-img-wrapper"><div class="fig-inline-img"><a href="https://www.medrxiv.org/content/medrxiv/early/2025/07/17/2025.07.17.25331211/F7.large.jpg?width=800&amp;height=600&amp;carousel=1" title="Pigmentation activity of BLOC1S1 variants (A) SDS-PAGE and immunoblot analysis of WT and BLOC1S1-KO MNT-1 cells using antibodies to the endogenous proteins indicated on the right. &#x3B1;-tubulin was used as a control. Two variants of BLOC1S1 are indicated by arrowheads. The positions of molecular mass markers (in kDa) are indicated on the left. (B) WT and BLOC1S1-KO MNT-1 cell pellets. Notice the lighter pigmentation of the KO cells. (C) Flow cytometry of WT and BLOC1S1-KO MNT-1 cells. The x-axis indicates the number of cells normalized to the mode (or peak) of the graph. The y-axis indicates side scatter area (SSC-A). (D) Bar graph representing the geometric mean &#xB1; SD values of the SSC-A parameter from three independent flow cytometry experiments like that shown in panel C. (E) Bar graph representing the light absorbance at 405 nm measured after melanin extraction. BLOC1S1-KO MNT-1 cells were rescued with lentiviruses carrying the indicated protein. WT and BLOC1S1-KO MNT-1 cells were used as controls. Data from five or six independent experiments are represented as the mean &#xB1; SD. Statistical significance was calculated by one-way ANOVA followed by multiple comparisons using Tukey&#x2019;s test. **P &lt; 0.005; ****P &lt; 0.0001; ns: not significant." class="highwire-fragment fragment-images colorbox-load" rel="gallery-fragment-images-638880100" data-figure-caption="&lt;div class=&quot;highwire-markup&quot;&gt;&lt;div xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml&quot;&gt;Pigmentation activity of &lt;em&gt;BLOC1S1&lt;/em&gt; variants &lt;strong&gt;(A)&lt;/strong&gt; SDS-PAGE and immunoblot analysis of WT and &lt;em&gt;BLOC1S1&lt;/em&gt;-KO MNT-1 cells using antibodies to the endogenous proteins indicated on the right. &#x3B1;-tubulin was used as a control. Two variants of <em>BLOC1S1</em> are indicated by arrowheads. The positions of molecular mass markers (in kDa) are indicated on the left. <strong>(B)</strong> WT and <em>BLOC1S1</em>-KO MNT-1 cell pellets. Notice the lighter pigmentation of the KO cells. <strong>(C)</strong> Flow cytometry of WT and <em>BLOC1S1</em>-KO MNT-1 cells. The x-axis indicates the number of cells normalized to the mode (or peak) of the graph. The y-axis indicates side scatter area (SSC-A). <strong>(D)</strong> Bar graph representing the geometric mean ± SD values of the SSC-A parameter from three independent flow cytometry experiments like that shown in panel C. <strong>(E)</strong> Bar graph representing the light absorbance at 405 nm measured after melanin extraction. <em>BLOC1S1</em>-KO MNT-1 cells were rescued with lentiviruses carrying the indicated protein. WT and <em>BLOC1S1</em>-KO MNT-1 cells were used as controls. Data from five or six independent experiments are represented as the mean ± SD. Statistical significance was calculated by one-way ANOVA followed by multiple comparisons using Tukey’s test. **<em>P</em> &lt; 0.005; ****<em>P</em> &lt; 0.0001; ns: not significant.</p><div class="sb-div caption-clear"></div></div></div></div></div><div class="section" id="sec-22"><h2 class="">Discussion</h2><p id="p-62">Herein, we present 11 individuals from seven unrelated families, including new phenotypics details for four previously reported individuals.<sup><a id="xref-ref-24-7" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-24">24</a></sup> All individuals are affected by a severe neurodevelopmental disorder and harbor biallelic variants of <em>BLOC1S1</em>. The disorder presents with early infantile onset and is characterized by deficient myelination, global developmental delay, intellectual disability, hypotonia, epilepsy, and visual impairment. The severity ranged from early death to a milder form with preserved ambulation and single-word communication. These neurological features are consistent with those recently described in individuals with pathogenic variants in <em>BORCS8.</em><sup><a id="xref-ref-19-9" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-19">19</a></sup> Given that both <em>BLOC1S1</em> and <em>BORCS8</em> encode subunits of the hetero-octameric BORC complex,<sup><a id="xref-ref-4-4" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-4">4</a></sup> these findings begin to define a broader clinical entity characterized by BORC deficiency.</p><p id="p-63">The visual impairment in individuals harboring <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants included bilateral optic atrophy in most individuals, and features of ocular albinism in two individuals (FIII:1 and FV:2). In addition, one individual had a pale complexion (FI:1) and one had hypopigmentation (FVII:1). The ocular albinism and pale complexion are reminiscent of those in HPS types 7, 8, 9 and 11 caused by variants in the <em>DTNBP1</em>, <em>BLOC1S3</em>, <em>BLOC1S6</em> and <em>BLOC1S5</em> genes, respectively.<sup><a id="xref-ref-41-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-41">41</a>,<a id="xref-ref-40-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-40">40</a>,<a id="xref-ref-42-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-42">42</a>,<a id="xref-ref-43-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-43">43</a>,<a id="xref-ref-44-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-44">44</a>,<a id="xref-ref-45-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-45">45</a>,<a id="xref-ref-46-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-46">46</a>,<a id="xref-ref-47-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-47">47</a>,<a id="xref-ref-48-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-48">48</a>,<a id="xref-ref-49-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-49">49</a>,<a id="xref-ref-50-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-50">50</a>,<a id="xref-ref-54-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-54">54</a>,<a id="xref-ref-51-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-51">51</a>,<a id="xref-ref-55-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-55">55</a>,<a id="xref-ref-52-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-52">52</a>,<a id="xref-ref-53-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-53">53</a></sup> All these genes encode subunits of the related hetero-octameric complex BLOC-1.<sup><a id="xref-ref-1-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-1">1</a>,<a id="xref-ref-2-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-2">2</a>,<a id="xref-ref-3-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-3">3</a></sup> These findings are consistent with BLOC1S1 being a subunit of BLOC-1<sup><a id="xref-ref-1-3" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-1">1</a>,<a id="xref-ref-2-3" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-2">2</a>,<a id="xref-ref-3-3" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-3">3</a></sup> in addition to BORC.<sup><a id="xref-ref-4-5" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-4">4</a></sup> However, the pigmentation defects in the individuals harboring <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants were notably milder than those in HPS, and other HPS features such as bleeding diathesis were not observed. These findings suggest that the <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants reported here have a more significant impact on BORC compared to BLOC-1. Thus, individuals with BLOC1S1 variants exhibit clinical and functional phenotypes more greatly impacted by BORC than BLOC-1 deficits.</p><p id="p-64">Three of the individuals from one family (FVII) described here had complete deletion of <em>BLOC1S1</em> and died on the first day after birth (FVII:1) or underwent pregnancy termination at 20 weeks and four days (FVII:2a and FVII:2b). However, these individuals also had complete deletions of three other neighboring genes, making it uncertain if their premature death was solely due to the deletion of <em>BLOC1S1</em>. In any event, this suggests that all the other <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants studied here are hypomorphic. The residual activity of these variants may be sufficient for the function of BLOC-1 in the biogenesis of LROs like melanosomes and platelet dense bodies, but insufficient for the function of BORC in the development of the central nervous system (CNS).</p><p id="p-65">Brain or neuronal defects have been reported in mice,<sup><a id="xref-ref-56-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-56">56</a></sup> Drosophila<sup><a id="xref-ref-57-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-57">57</a></sup> and <em>C. elegans,</em><sup><a id="xref-ref-60-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-60">60</a></sup> and defective pigmentation has been observed in mice,<sup><a id="xref-ref-56-3" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-56">56</a></sup> Drosophila<sup><a id="xref-ref-57-3" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-57">57</a></sup> and zebrafish,<sup><a id="xref-ref-58-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-58">58</a></sup> with KO or variants in <em>BLOC1S1</em> orthologs. These findings indicate that the role of <em>BLOC1S1</em> in neurodevelopment and pigmentation is broadly conserved across metazoans. However, the effects of <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants had not been previously described in human cells. Our experiments demonstrate that KO of <em>BLOC1S1</em> in human HeLa cells leads to redistribution of lysosomes towards the perinuclear cytoplasm and increased levels of the autophagy marker LC3-II. These phenotypes are characteristic of defective BORC/ARL8-dependent coupling of lysosomes to kinesins 1 and 3<sup><a id="xref-ref-4-6" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-4">4</a>,<a id="xref-ref-16-3" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-16">16</a></sup> and to the HOPS complex,<sup><a id="xref-ref-20-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-20">20</a>,<a id="xref-ref-21-4" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-21">21</a></sup> respectively. Moreover, we found that <em>BLOC1S1</em> KO in human iPSC-derived neurons reduced the transport of lysosomal vesicles into the axon, also consistent with the role of BORC and ARL8 in mediating kinesin-driven transport of these organelles into the axon.<sup><a id="xref-ref-18-3" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-18">18</a>,<a id="xref-ref-19-10" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-19">19</a>,<a id="xref-ref-61-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-61">61</a></sup> Additionally, we observed increased levels of neuronal LC3-II, with particularly pronounced accumulation in aberrant swellings along the axon shaft. These swellings were filled with the microtubule protein tau and the neurofilament protein NFH, all characteristics of axonal dystrophy or degeneration.<sup><a id="xref-ref-62-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-62">62</a>,<a id="xref-ref-63-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-63">63</a></sup> These neuronal defects may thus contribute to the neurodevelopmental aspects of the disease.</p><p id="p-66">While <em>BLOC1S1</em> KO in human cells served as a model for the <em>BLOC1S1</em>-deletion in FVII:1, FVII:2 and FVII:3 individuals, the rescue of peripheral lysosome distribution and basal LC3-II levels in HeLa cells was used to assess the properties of several frameshift or missense variants. We found that all the tested variants exhibited varying defects in expression, assembly, lysosome dispersal and/or autophagy. Among them, the frameshift variant E49* showed the most severe deficiencies, with little to no activity in all assays. The missense variants demonstrated defects in one or more of the assessed parameters, including expression, assembly and/or function. These findings provide relevant evidence in favor of the pathogenicity of all the tested variants.<sup><a id="xref-ref-30-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-30">30</a>,<a id="xref-ref-31-2" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-31">31</a></sup></p><p id="p-67"><em>BLOC1S1</em> KO in the human melanocytic cell line MNT-1 also resulted in reduced pigmentation. The observation that the individuals harboring <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants had only mild or no pigmentation defects supports the conclusion that their <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants retain sufficient activity to maintain melanosome development, albeit with some reduction. This is consistent with the ability of all identified <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants to completely or partially rescue the reduced pigmentation of <em>BLOC1S1</em>-KO MNT-1 cells. Mice with heart- or liver-specific KO of <em>Bloc1s1</em> exhibit defects in the corresponding organs.<sup><a id="xref-ref-64-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-64">64</a>,<a id="xref-ref-65-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-65">65</a>,<a id="xref-ref-66-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-66">66</a>,<a id="xref-ref-67-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-67">67</a>,<a id="xref-ref-68-1" class="xref-bibr" href="#ref-68">68</a></sup> However, individuals harboring <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants exhibited no obvious cardiac or hepatic defects, suggesting that the <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants retain sufficient activity in these organs as well. Predominant neurological presentation in <em>BLOC1S1</em>-associated human disease may reflect the greater vulnerability of neurons and possibly glial cells to disruptions in intracellular protein and organelle trafficking.</p><p id="p-68">In conclusion, we expand BORC-associated disease through the description of 11 subjects with <em>BLOC1S1</em> relevant biallelic variants. Individuals harboring <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants have a primarily neurologic phenotype of early infantile onset developmental delay, with intellectual and motor impairments. Clinical course is complicated by epilepsy and early mortality. In addition, individuals harboring <em>BLOC1S1</em> variants have profound CNS hypomyelination. A subset of individuals also show features of mild oculocutaneous albinism, which is explained by the dual role of the BLOC1S1 subunit in BLOC-1 and BORC. Altogether, our clinical and functional studies establish BLOC1S1 bi-allelic variants as a new genetic cause of a lysosomal disorder characterized by hypomyelinating leukodystrophy with epileptic encephalopathy.</p></div><div class="section" id="sec-23"><h2 class="">Declaration of interests</h2><p id="p-69">The authors declare no competing interests. EW is CSO and equity holder of “The Organoid Company”. class="cit-auth"><span class="cit-name-surname">Pu</span>,  <span class="cit-name-given-names">J.</span></span>, <span class="cit-auth"><span class="cit-name-surname">Schindler</span>,  <span class="cit-name-given-names">C.</span></span>, <span class="cit-auth"><span class="cit-name-surname">Jia</span>,  <span class="cit-name-given-names">R.</span></span>, <span class="cit-auth"><span (<span class="cit-pub-date">2015</span>). <span class="cit-article-title">BORC, a multisubunit complex that regulates lysosome positioning</span>. <abbr class="cit-jnl-abbrev">Dev Cell</abbr> <span class="cit-vol">33</span>, <span class="cit-fpage">176</span>–<span class="cit-lpage">188</span>.</cite></div><div class="cit-extra"><a class="cit-ref-sprinkles cit-ref-sprinkles-openurl cit-ref-sprinkles-open-url"><span>OpenUrl</span></a><a href="/lookup/external-ref?access_num=10.1016/j.devcel.2015.02.011&amp;link_type=DOI"
